<p><b>Romelu Menama Lukaku Bolingoli</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[romelu lukaku]</a></span>; born 13 May 1993) is a Belgian professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> club <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium national team</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, he began his professional career at <a href="/wiki/Belgian_First_Division_A" title="Belgian First Division A">Belgian Pro League</a> club <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a> in 2009, where he made his senior debut, at age 16. He won the league's top goalscorer, the league championship and the <a href="/wiki/Ebony_Shoe" title="Ebony Shoe">Belgian Ebony Shoe</a> there. He signed for English side <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in 2011, but featured sparingly in his first season and joined <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on loan in 2012. He helped them to an unexpected eighth-place finish in the 2012–13 season and ahead of the 2013–14 season, he joined <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on loan. After helping Everton reach a club-record points tally, he joined the team in a permanent deal worth a club-record fee of £28 million in 2014. He was named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year_(2010s)#Premier_League_8" title="PFA Team of the Year (2010s)">2016–17</a> <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a>, Lukaku signed for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in 2017, for an initial fee of £75 million.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> After two seasons in Manchester Lukaku's relationship with the club deteriorated. Lukaku failed to return for pre-season training, was fined, and subsequently signed for <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> in August 2019, for a reported club record €80 million.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A Belgian international, Lukaku has played 89 games for his country, and scored 57 goals, making him <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team_records_and_statistics#General_2" title="Belgium national football team records and statistics">Belgium's all-time top goalscorer</a>.<sup id="ref_N1_1" class="reference"><a href="#cnote_N1">[N1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku made his senior international debut for Belgium in 2010, at age 17, and has since represented his country at three major tournaments, including two <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA European Championship</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a>, Lukaku led Belgium to a third-place finish by finishing as the joint second-highest goalscorer, and won the Bronze Boot.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<p>Lukaku joined his local team <a href="/wiki/K._Rupel_Boom_F.C." title="K. Rupel Boom F.C.">Rupel Boom</a> at age five. After four seasons at Rupel Boom, Lukaku was discovered by scouts of <a href="/wiki/Lierse_S.K." title="Lierse S.K.">Lierse</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Belgian_First_Division_A" title="Belgian First Division A">Belgian Pro League</a> club with an established youth academy. He played for Lierse from 2004 until 2006, scoring 121 goals in 68 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-LukakuYouth_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LukakuYouth-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> After Lierse were relegated from the Belgian Pro League, <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a> purchased 13 youth players from Lierse in the 2006 mid-season, including Lukaku. He played three more years as a youth player with Anderlecht, scoring 131 goals in 93 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anderlecht">Anderlecht</span></h3>
<p>When Lukaku turned 16 on 13 May 2009, he signed a professional contract with Anderlecht lasting until 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Eleven days later, he made his Belgian First Division debut on 24 May 2009 in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Belgian_First_Division#Championship_playoff" title="2008–09 Belgian First Division">championship play-off</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Standard_Li%C3%A8ge" title="Standard Liège">Standard Liège</a> as a 69th-minute <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">defender</a> <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Bern%C3%A1rdez" title="Víctor Bernárdez">Víctor Bernárdez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-StandardBelgi_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StandardBelgi-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Anderlecht lost the match 1–0. Lukaku became a regular member of Anderlecht's first team during the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_R.S.C._Anderlecht_season" title="2009–10 R.S.C. Anderlecht season">2009–10 season</a>, scoring his first goal at senior level against <a href="/wiki/S.V._Zulte_Waregem" title="S.V. Zulte Waregem">Zulte Waregem</a> in the 89th minute after coming on as substitute for <a href="/wiki/Rubenilson_dos_Santos_da_Rocha" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubenilson dos Santos da Rocha">Kanu</a> on 28 August 2009. "After scoring I dived into a sea of happiness," he told Berend Scholten from UEFA.com. "You think you are flying and can take on the whole world."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He ended the season as the top goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Belgian_Pro_League" title="2009–10 Belgian Pro League">Pro League</a> with 15 goals as Anderlecht won its 30th <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgian_football_champions" title="List of Belgian football champions">Belgian title</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-punches_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punches-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He also scored four goals during the club's run to the last 16 of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2009–10 UEFA Europa League">2009–10 UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-punches_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punches-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Belgian_Pro_League" title="2010–11 Belgian Pro League">2010–11 season</a>, Lukaku scored 20 goals in all competitions, but Anderlecht failed to retain their league title despite finishing top of the table during the regular season.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea">Chelsea</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg/140px-Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg/210px-Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg/280px-Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4167" data-file-height="8451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_Chelsea_vs_AS-Roma_10AUG2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku warming up for <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer">Transfer</span></h4>
<p>In August 2011, Lukaku joined <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> for a fee reported to be around €12&#160;million (£10&#160;million), rising to €20&#160;million (£17&#160;million) in add-ons. Lukaku was given the number 18 shirt and signed a five-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2011.E2.80.9312_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–12_season">2011–12 season</span></h4>
<p>Lukaku made his debut at Stamford Bridge in a 3–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> in the 83rd minute, coming on as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku made his first start for Chelsea in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Football_League_Cup" title="2011–12 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>. Chelsea went on to win the match on <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout" title="Penalty shootout">penalties</a>. He spent the majority of the season playing for the <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelsea F.C. Reserves and Academy">reserves</a> and started his first Premier League match on 13 May 2012, against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>, and turned in a <a href="/wiki/Player_of_the_match" title="Player of the match">man of the match</a> performance, providing an <a href="/wiki/Assist_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Assist (football)">assist</a> for <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a>'s opener.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> However, Lukaku stressed he was disappointed with his involvement at the end of his debut season, revealing that, after his side's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> win in <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2012 UEFA Champions League Final">the final</a> on 19 May, he refused to hold the trophy, explaining "it wasn't me, but my team that won".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9313_season:_Loan_to_West_Bromwich_Albion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–13_season:_Loan_to_West_Bromwich_Albion">2012–13 season: Loan to West Bromwich Albion</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg/140px-Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg/210px-Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg/280px-Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="1534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_kick_off_Fulham_v_WBA_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku playing for <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> in 2012</div></div></div>
<p>After speculation linking Lukaku to a loan move to <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> on 10 August 2012, he joined <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on a season-long loan deal.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first league goal eight days later, coming on as a substitute in the 77th minute in a 3–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He made his full debut in a win against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Hawthorns" title="The Hawthorns">The Hawthorns</a>, scoring the match's only goal.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On 24 November, Lukaku came on as a 70th-minute substitute for <a href="/wiki/Shane_Long" title="Shane Long">Shane Long</a> and netted a penalty and provided an assist to <a href="/wiki/Marc-Antoine_Fortun%C3%A9" title="Marc-Antoine Fortuné">Marc-Antoine Fortuné</a>, as West Brom defeated <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> 4–2 away at the <a href="/wiki/Stadium_of_Light" title="Stadium of Light">Stadium of Light</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The win proved to be West Brom's fourth consecutive win in the top flight for the first time since 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 12 January 2013, Lukaku had his first multi-goal game in the Premier League, giving West Brom a 0–2 lead against Reading, before a late comeback gave the Berkshire club a 3–2 victory at the <a href="/wiki/Madejski_Stadium" title="Madejski Stadium">Madejski Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In the face of claims he wanted to stay with West Brom for another year, Lukaku confirmed to the press he still wished to become a legend at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 11 February, Lukaku came on as a substitute and scored his tenth Premier League goal of the season against Liverpool in a match that ended 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He scored his second brace of the campaign, scoring both goals for West Brom in their 2–1 home defeat of Sunderland on 23 February.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 9 March, in a league match against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, Lukaku scored the equalising goal before having a penalty kick saved; West Brom eventually won the game courtesy of a <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_de_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Jonathan de Guzmán">Jonathan de Guzmán</a> own goal.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On 19 May, coming on as a second-half substitute, Lukaku scored a remarkable second-half <a href="/wiki/Perfect_hat-trick" class="mw-redirect" title="Perfect hat-trick">perfect</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_hat-tricks" title="List of Premier League hat-tricks">hat-trick</a>, as West Brom came from three goals down to draw 5–5 in the season's final home match against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The match was <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a>'s 1,500th and last match in charge of United, and the highest-scoring draw in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_records_and_statistics" title="Premier League records and statistics">Premier League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Despite being loaned out by the club, Lukaku outscored all of his Chelsea teammates in the Premier League that season, being the sixth-highest goal scorer of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Premier_League" title="2012–13 Premier League">2012–13 season</a> with 17 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku played two Premier League matches for Chelsea at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Chelsea F.C. season">2013–14 season</a>. He also came on as a substitute in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2013 UEFA Super Cup">2013 UEFA Super Cup</a>, ultimately missing the deciding penalty in the shootout as <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Neuer" title="Manuel Neuer">Manuel Neuer</a> saved his shot and Chelsea lost to <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314_season:_Loan_to_Everton"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14_season:_Loan_to_Everton">2013–14 season: Loan to Everton</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg/170px-Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg/255px-Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg/340px-Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1817" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_2014-05-03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku pre-match with <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>On the final day of the summer 2013 transfer window, Lukaku joined <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on a season-long loan.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The striker made his début for the Toffees away to <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> on 21 September 2013, scoring the winning goal in a 3–2 victory for Everton. During the header, he had a collision with a West Ham defender and was taken off the pitch for some treatment. The physio had to tell him he had scored the winner.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He scored twice on his home debut nine days later in a 3–2 win against <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, as well assisting <a href="/wiki/Ross_Barkley" title="Ross Barkley">Ross Barkley</a>'s goal.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He then opened the scoring in a 3–1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in the following match.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He continued his impressive start at the club by netting the opening goal in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, and then scored twice in the first <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a> of the season as Everton drew 3–3 against Liverpool, with Lukaku stating afterwards it was the best experience he has had in his short career.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2014, Lukaku was named by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> as one of the ten most promising young players in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-top10list_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top10list-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> but later in the month was taken off on a stretcher with an ankle ligament damage after <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Barry" title="Gareth Barry">Gareth Barry</a> slipped and slid into the striker as he attempted to block <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>'s opening goal in the Merseyside derby against Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku made his return from injury against West Ham in March 2014, scoring the only goal of the match on the 81st minute after coming on as a second-half substitute.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On 6 April, he scored one goal and assisted another as Everton beat <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> 3–0 at <a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">Goodison Park</a> to record a sixth consecutive Premier League win.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> His final goal for the loan period came on the last day of the season as he scored the second in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku found the net 15 times in 31 league matches to help Everton to fifth place with a club record of 72 Premier League points.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Everton">Everton</span></h3>
<h4><span id="Transfer_and_2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_and_2014–15_season">Transfer and 2014–15 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_(16869431132)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/270px-Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_%2816869431132%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_vs_Dinamo_Kyiv_(16869431132)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku playing for Everton in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Lukaku signed a five-year deal with Everton in July 2014 for a club record fee of £28&#160;million, and he was assigned the number 10 shirt.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal as a permanent player on 13 September, against his former club West Brom. Lukaku <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration#Notable_non-celebrations" title="Goal celebration">did not celebrate the goal</a>, and was applauded by the West Brom fans for his sign of respect. On 19 February 2015, Lukaku scored his first Everton hat-trick in a 4–1 win for Everton against <a href="/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys" title="BSC Young Boys">BSC Young Boys</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> last 32; he struck with a header, a right-foot shot and a left-foot shot.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> He added another two goals in a 3–1 win in the second leg a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> With eight goals, he was the tournament's joint highest scorer that season, alongside <a href="/wiki/Alan_Carvalho" title="Alan Carvalho">Alan</a> of <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">red Bull Salzburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season">2015–16 season</span></h4>
<p>In the second game of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16 Premier League</a> season, Lukaku scored a first-half double in Everton's 0–3 win at <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> on 15 August 2015 with his first two shots on target. Before the match, he presented a T-shirt to a home fan whom he had accidentally struck with the ball during shooting practice.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 26 August, he scored another brace in a 5–3 extra-time win over <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a> side <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Football_League_Cup" title="2015–16 Football League Cup">League Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 28 September, Lukaku scored twice and assisted the other against West Brom as he managed to guide his team from losing 2–0 to winning 2–3.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He scored against Liverpool the following week in a 1–1 draw at Goodison Park.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 21 November, Lukaku scored twice in a 4–0 win over Aston Villa, becoming the fifth player under 23 years of age to score at least 50 Premier League goals, after <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-becomes_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-becomes-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On 7 December, Lukaku scored a close-range goal in a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>, his 50th in 100 appearances in all competitions for Everton.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 12 December, Lukaku became the first Everton player to score in six consecutive Premier League matches, and the first to score in seven consecutive matches in all competitions since <a href="/wiki/Bob_Latchford" title="Bob Latchford">Bob Latchford</a> 40 years previously, when he opened the scoring in the <i>Toffees'</i> 1–1 draw with Norwich City at <a href="/wiki/Carrow_Road" title="Carrow Road">Carrow Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In his next match, a 3–2 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, Lukaku became the first Everton player since <a href="/wiki/Dave_Hickson" title="Dave Hickson">Dave Hickson</a> in 1954 to score in eight consecutive matches.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 February 2016, Lukaku scored his 20th goal of the season in a 0–3 victory at <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a>, meaning he was the first Everton player since <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Sharp" title="Graeme Sharp">Graeme Sharp</a> to score at least 20 goals in all competitions in consecutive seasons for Everton. The strike was also his 16th league goal of the season, equalling Premier League goal scoring records for Everton set by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Cottee" title="Tony Cottee">Tony Cottee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Kanchelskis" title="Andrei Kanchelskis">Andrei Kanchelskis</a> in the mid-1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku followed this goal with another strike in a 0–2 victory at <a href="/wiki/AFC_Bournemouth" title="AFC Bournemouth">AFC Bournemouth</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dean_Court" title="Dean Court">Dean Court</a> for his 21st goal of the season. This victory sent Everton into the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FA_Cup" title="2015–16 FA Cup">FA Cup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and equalled the number of goals scored in all competitions by <a href="/wiki/Yakubu_(footballer)" title="Yakubu (footballer)">Yakubu</a> for Everton in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Everton_F.C._season" title="2007–08 Everton F.C. season">2007–08 season</a>, the previous best in the Premier League era.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 1 March, Lukaku scored in a 1–3 victory against Aston Villa at <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a>, his 17th league goal of the season, a Premier League-era record for Everton.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The goal also meant Lukaku had equalled his previous best goal return in a league season, set during his loan spell at West Brom in the 2012–13 season.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season">2016–17 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_United_v_Everton,_April_2017_(06).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG/220px-Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG/330px-Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG/440px-Manchester_United_v_Everton%2C_April_2017_%2806%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_United_v_Everton,_April_2017_(06).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku with Everton in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>On 12 September 2016, Lukaku scored his first goals of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Everton_F.C._season" title="2016–17 Everton F.C. season">2016–17 season</a> with all three goals in a 3–0 against Sunderland at the Stadium of Light. His goals were scored in 11 minutes and 37 seconds, making it the 12th-fastest hat-trick in Premier League history.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On 4 February 2017, Lukaku scored four goals, the first of which was Everton's fastest ever Premier League goal, against Bournemouth in a 6–3 victory at Goodison Park.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It was also the 300th hat-trick scored in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 25 February 2017, he equalled <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Ferguson" title="Duncan Ferguson">Duncan Ferguson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_Everton_F.C._records_and_statistics" title="List of Everton F.C. records and statistics">club record</a> for Premier League goals, scoring his 60th EPL goal for the Toffees in a 2–0 victory over Sunderland at Goodison Park.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On 5 March, he surpassed Ferguson to become the outright record holder, scoring in a 3–2 loss against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> away at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In the next match, a 3–0 home win against West Brom, Lukaku scored to become the first Everton player since Bob Latchford to score 20 or more goals in all competitions for three consecutive seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> A week later, during a 4–0 victory over Hull City, he scored twice to take his league goals tally to 21 for the season, thereby becoming the first Everton player since <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> 31 years previously to surpass 20 league goals in a season, as well as being the fourth player and first foreign player to score 80 Premier League goals before the age of 24.<sup id="cite_ref-eighty_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eighty-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2017, Lukaku turned down a new five-year contract worth a reported £140,000 a week amidst rumours of a return to Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In an interview, he questioned the club's ambition to make big transfers and chase Champions League qualification, offending his manager <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> A goal in a 3–1 win for Everton against <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> on 15 April meant Lukaku was the first Everton player since Bob Latchford to score 25 goals in two consecutive seasons in all competitions, and the first player since the legendary <a href="/wiki/Dixie_Dean" title="Dixie Dean">Dixie Dean</a> to score in nine consecutive matches at Goodison Park.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April 2017, Lukaku was named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1617_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1617-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He was also included in the six player shortlists for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Players%27_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Players&#39; Player of the Year">PFA Players' Player of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> awards.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_2">Transfer</span></h4>
<p>Lukaku joined Manchester United on 10 July 2017, signing a five-year contract with the option of a further year.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Although the fee was officially undisclosed, it was reported to be worth an initial £75&#160;million, plus £15&#160;million in add-ons.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Thus, he became a teammate with his French-speaking close friend <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pogba" title="Paul Pogba">Paul Pogba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku's signing came a day after former Manchester United captain <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> left the club to return to Everton, Rooney's boyhood club.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Manchester United F.C. season">2017–18 season</a>, Lukaku asked the permission of <a href="/wiki/Zlatan_Ibrahimovi%C4%87" title="Zlatan Ibrahimovi">Zlatan Ibrahimovi</a> if he could take over the number 9 shirt from him.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku was confirmed to have been given the number on 14 July.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season">2017–18 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg/170px-Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg/255px-Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg/340px-Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="440" data-file-height="580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romelu_Lukaku_27_September_2017_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku playing for Manchester United in the UEFA Champions League in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Lukaku made his debut against <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a> on 8 August in the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2017 UEFA Super Cup">2017 UEFA Super Cup</a>, and scored his first competitive goal for the club in a 2–1 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> His league debut came five days later at home to West Ham. Lukaku scored twice in a 4–0 win,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> becoming the fourth Manchester United player to score two goals on his Premier League debut for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On 12 September, he scored his first <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> goal in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On 17 September, Lukaku scored United's third goal in a 4–0 win over his former club Everton, with Lukaku running over towards Everton fans and cupping his ears during his <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration" title="Goal celebration">goal celebration</a> in response to being booed throughout the game.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On 27 September, Lukaku scored twice in a 4–1 win over <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a>, taking his tally to 10 goals in his first nine appearances. In doing so, he broke the record set by <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Sir Bobby Charlton</a> who had scored nine goals in his first nine appearances for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In a 2–1 win over his former club Chelsea on 25 February 2018, Lukaku scored the equaliser and then assisted <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Lingard" title="Jesse Lingard">Jesse Lingard</a>'s game-winning goal.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> He scored his 200th goal for club and country on 13 March in a 2–1 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> that eliminated Manchester United from the Champions League in the round of 16.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On 31 March 2018, Lukaku scored to open a 2–0 home win over Swansea. It was his <a href="/wiki/List_of_footballers_with_100_or_more_Premier_League_goals" title="List of footballers with 100 or more Premier League goals">100th Premier League goal</a> in his 216th game, and made him the fifth youngest of the 28 players to reach the tally.<sup id="cite_ref-sky100_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sky100-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season">2018–19 season</span></h4>
<p>Lukaku started the 2018–19 season with four goals in his first five appearances, including a brace against <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, before a 12-game drought lasting from 19 September to 27 November 2018. Goals against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> followed before the sacking of manager <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>, only for Mourinho's replacement – former United striker <a href="/wiki/Ole_Gunnar_Solskj%C3%A6r" title="Ole Gunnar Solskjær">Ole Gunnar Solskjær</a> – to leave Lukaku out of the squad entirely for his first two games in charge against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>. Lukaku made substitute appearances in United's next two games against <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" class="mw-redirect" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> scoring in both matches within two minutes of coming on. He then played the full 90 minutes of the FA Cup third round tie against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a>, scoring the second goal in a 2–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> However, Solskjær continued to prefer to start <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Rashford" title="Marcus Rashford">Marcus Rashford</a> up front and Lukaku started just five of the next nine games, playing the full 90 minutes in just two and failing to score in any of them. His goalscoring form returned for the next three games, as he scored braces against each of <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Southampton<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a>. The goals against PSG were part of a 3–1 win that saw United through to the Champions League quarter-finals on the away goals rule, the first time any team had progressed after losing at home in the first leg by two goals or more.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> However, United were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in the quarterfinals 4–0 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter_Milan">Inter Milan</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season">2019–20 season</span></h4>
<p>Lukaku joined Italian club <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> on 8 August 2019, signing a five-year contract for a fee reported to be a club record €80&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> He later mentioned the reasons for leaving Manchester United, by claiming that he was made a scapegoat alongside other players such as Paul Pogba and <a href="/wiki/Alexis_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Alexis Sánchez">Alexis Sánchez</a>, in addition to club's failure to protect him against rumours about his future.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> However, Lukaku made his debut for Inter Milan on 26 August in the opening <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> matchday against <a href="/wiki/U.S._Lecce" title="U.S. Lecce">Lecce</a>, netting his side's third goal with his first shot in a 4–0 home win.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The goal meant that Lukaku has found the net in his first league game for five of the six clubs he has represented; Anderlecht, West Brom, Everton, Manchester United, and Inter;<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> he also become only the third Belgian to score for Inter in Serie A, after <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Scifo" title="Enzo Scifo">Enzo Scifo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radja_Nainggolan" title="Radja Nainggolan">Radja Nainggolan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In the club's second league game of the season at <a href="/wiki/Cagliari_Calcio" title="Cagliari Calcio">Cagliari</a> on 1 September, Lukaku scored the match-winning goal from the penalty spot to give Inter a 2–1 victory away from home; however, he was subject to <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_association_football" title="Racism in association football">racial abuse</a> from some of the Cagliari fans.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first months since his arrival, Lukaku formed an attacking partnership with Argentine youngster <a href="/wiki/Lautaro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Lautaro Martínez">Lautaro Martínez</a>, dubbed "Lu-La" by Italian media.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> This became after the duo scored a brace each in the 4–3 away win against <a href="/wiki/U.S._Sassuolo_Calcio" title="U.S. Sassuolo Calcio">Sassuolo</a> in October, giving Inter the first triumph since 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On 2 November, Lukaku scored a brace in a 2–1 away win over <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a> in Serie A, which saw him match <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>'s record of nine goals in his first 11 league appearances for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> On 27 November, Lukaku scored his first <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> goal for Inter in a 3–1 away win against <a href="/wiki/SK_Slavia_Prague" title="SK Slavia Prague">Slavia Prague</a> in the group stage; in addition to that, he also assisted the two other goals scored by Lautaro Martínez and had two goals disallowed himself.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In the final match home against Barcelona, Lukaku scored his side's only goal in a 2–1 defeat, meaning that Inter was transferred to Europa League for the second season in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He begun the new year on 6 January by scoring a brace in a 3–1 win against <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>, giving Inter the first league win at <a href="/wiki/Stadio_San_Paolo" title="Stadio San Paolo">Stadio San Paolo</a> since October 1997;<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> he earned praise from the media for his first goal scored in the 14th minute, which came from an individual effort.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On 9 February, Lukaku scored the final goal of the 4–2 home win over <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Madonnina" title="Derby della Madonnina">cross-town rivals</a> <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, sending Inter to the top of the table and giving them another double over Milan; it was also his 17th league goal of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 July, Lukaku scored a brace in a 3–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Genoa_C.F.C." title="Genoa C.F.C.">Genoa</a>; in doing so, he became the first Inter player since <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Nyers" title="István Nyers">István Nyers</a> in 1949–50 season to score 15 away goals in a Serie A season, and the first do to so in his debut season.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> He concluded his first Serie A season with 23 goals, as Inter finished runner-up by just one point to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the standings; only Ronaldo (25) and Nyers (26) have scored more than him in their debut season at Inter.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 5 August, Lukaku scored in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Getafe_CF" title="Getafe CF">Getafe</a> in the Europa League's round of 16, helping his side reach the quarter-finals of a European competition for the first time since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> It was his 30th goal in all competitions, a new personal best, and he had also scored for the 8th consecutive Europa League match, equalling the all-time record set by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> in 2004–05.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In the quarter-finals on 10 August, he broke the record, scoring in his ninth consecutive match in the competition in a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> in Düsseldorf, to send Inter into the semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On 17 August, Lukaku scored a brace in a 5–0 win against <a href="/wiki/FC_Shakhtar_Donetsk" title="FC Shakhtar Donetsk">Shakhtar Donetsk</a>—his tenth consecutive match in the competition—as Inter reached the <a href="/wiki/2020_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2020 UEFA Europa League Final">final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In the final, he earned and scored a penalty in the 5th minute, but also scored an own goal in the 74th minute, which was eventually the winning goal for <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> in a 3–2 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> However, Lukaku managed to equal <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>'s record in 1997–98 season, by scoring 34 goals in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season">2020–21 season</span></h4>
<p>On 21 October 2020, Lukaku scored a brace in a 2–2 draw against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> in the first match of the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2020–21 UEFA Champions League">2020–21 UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> On 1 December, he scored another brace against Borussia Mönchengladbach to secure a 3–2 away win.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> However, Inter drew their last match against Shakhtar Donetsk, to finish last in their group and to be eliminated from all European competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 January 2021, Lukaku scored a goal in a 6–2 win over <a href="/wiki/F.C._Crotone" title="F.C. Crotone">Crotone</a>, to reach his 50th goal across all competitions in only 70 matches, breaking the previous record of Ronaldo who scored 50 goals in 77 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> On 14 February, he scored a brace and got an assist against <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> in a 3–1 victory, bringing his Serie A tally to 16 goals for the season and equalling <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> as the league's top scorer. Lukaku's second goal was also the 300th of his professional career.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:147px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/145px-Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="145" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/218px-Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/290px-Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="458" data-file-height="661" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lukaku_Belgium_National_Team_vs_USA_2013_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku with <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> in May 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Lukaku was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_under-21_football_team" title="Belgium national under-21 football team">Belgium under-21 team</a> and scored a goal on his debut against <a href="/wiki/Slovenia_national_under-21_football_team" title="Slovenia national under-21 football team">Slovenia</a>. On 24 February 2010, Lukaku was named for the first time in the <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium senior squad</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On 17 November 2010, he scored his first two international goals in a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku scored his first goal in almost two years for the national team, netting the winner in a 4–2 friendly victory over rivals the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> on 15 August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 October 2013, Lukaku scored two goals as Belgium defeated Croatia 2–1 to secure a place in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In May 2014, Lukaku was named in Belgium's squad for the 2014 World Cup. On 26 May, he scored his first international hat-trick in a pre-tournament friendly against neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> However, as Belgium made seven <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitutions</a> during this match instead of the permitted six, it was not recognised as an official match by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HLN040614_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLN040614-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June, he scored first of Belgium's two goals in the 2–0 victory in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In Belgium's first match of the tournament, a 2–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, Lukaku started and played 58 minutes before being replaced by <a href="/wiki/Divock_Origi" title="Divock Origi">Divock Origi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Round_of_16" title="2014 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">round of 16</a>, Lukaku came on as a substitute prior to <a href="/wiki/Overtime#Association_football" title="Overtime">extra time</a> and assisted <a href="/wiki/Kevin_De_Bruyne" title="Kevin De Bruyne">Kevin De Bruyne</a>'s opening goal three minutes later. In the 105th minute, he scored his first goal of the tournament as Belgium defeated the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a> 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:147px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg/145px-2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg" decoding="async" width="145" height="339" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg/218px-2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg/290px-2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="2388" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_RUS_v_BEL_exhibition_-_Romelu_Lukaku.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku playing for Belgium against <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> in March 2017</div></div></div>
<p>On 29 March 2016, Lukaku headed a consolation in a 2–1 loss away to <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>, assisted by his brother, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Lukaku" title="Jordan Lukaku">Jordan Lukaku</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>, Lukaku scored twice in Belgium's 3–0 second group stage match win on 18 June 2016 over the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 November 2017, Lukaku equalled the all-time Belgium goalscoring record set by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Voorhoof" title="Bernard Voorhoof">Bernard Voorhoof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_van_Himst" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul van Himst">Paul van Himst</a> after scoring twice against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> in a 3–3 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Four days after he equalled the record, Lukaku became Belgium's all-time record goalscorer with 31 international goals at the age of 24 after he scored the only goal in a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Although this record was counted by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Belgian_Football_Association" title="Royal Belgian Football Association">Royal Belgian Football Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-KBVBdata_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KBVBdata-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> FIFA only officially recognised 28 goals after a nullified international friendly match against Luxembourg on 26 May 2014 which he netted a hat trick in a 5–1 win because the former Belgium coach, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Wilmots" title="Marc Wilmots">Marc Wilmots</a> made seven substitutions during the match instead of the permitted six which are not in accordance to the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">Laws of the Game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 June 2018, Lukaku officially became Belgium's all-time leading scorer with 31 goals after scoring a goal in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a>. He also broke a three-way tie with the previous record goalscorers, Bernard Voorhoof and Paul Van Himst.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:147px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bel-Tun_(15).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg/145px-Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="145" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg/218px-Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg/290px-Bel-Tun_%2815%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="999" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bel-Tun_(15).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lukaku (right) playing against Tunisia in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 18 June 2018, Lukaku scored twice in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_football_team" title="Panama national football team">Panama</a> in their opening group game at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> In the next group game on 23 June 2018, he scored twice again in a 5–2 win over <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, Lukaku became the first player since <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a> in 1986 to score two goals or more in consecutive World Cup matches.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> He eventually ended the tournament with four goals and one assist, which earned him the Bronze Boot award, as Belgium finished the tournament in third place.<sup id="cite_ref-bronze_boot_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bronze_boot-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 October 2019, Lukaku scored his 50th and 51st international goals in a 9–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying">Euro 2020 qualifier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>Lukaku is a left-footed player,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> who in 2014 was named by <i>The Guardian</i> as one of the ten most promising young players in Europe. A large and physically powerful striker, with an eye for goal, Lukaku has been known to use his physicality to get around defenders.<sup id="cite_ref-top10list_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top10list-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> However, despite his size, strength, physical build, and ability to hold-up play with his back to goal, his favoured role is not as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Centre-forward" title="Forward (association football)">target-man in the centre</a>, but as an out-and-out <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> or poacher; due to his tactical versatility, he is also capable of playing as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Winger" title="Forward (association football)">winger</a>. A well-rounded <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>, who is also strong in the air, beyond his physical qualities and goalscoring ability, he possesses pace, athleticism, awareness, good link-up play, technical attributes, and vision, as well as an ability to get into good attacking positions or create space for teammates with his intelligent runs off the ball. Although he was once criticised by pundits for his limited defensive contribution, he has since been praised by his managers for his work-rate off the ball. However, despite his ability, he has also come into criticism in the media at times over his movement, first touch, finishing, and overall consistency.<sup id="cite_ref-paradox_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paradox-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>In a 2016 interview with <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, Lukaku named <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a> as the two strikers who made him want to play for Chelsea, but it was the mention of a third striker during the interview, his ultimate idol <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, that lit him up with excitement, with Lukaku stating,
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"Ronaldo changed football. He was the one you would look at. You would see him doing <a href="/wiki/Step_over" title="Step over">step-overs</a> and you were thinking: 'Who does this?' You would see defenders falling over and you were like: 'Wow.' The goals that he scored, and at crucial times. He scored goals where you were like: 'Oh man, this is not serious.'"</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Lukaku speaking to ESPN on his idol, Ronaldo.<sup id="cite_ref-idol_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idol-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<p>Crediting the former Brazilian striker as his major influence as a kid, Lukaku added, "He changed the dimension of a striker. He was fast, he can <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribble</a> like a winger, run like a sprinter, he was as strong as an ox".<sup id="cite_ref-idol_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idol-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> His devotion to Ronaldo is such that he finds the time to search <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> for videos of him. When mentioned that he shares certain characteristics with the Brazilian, Lukaku responded, "Be like Ronaldo? There is only one Ronaldo".<sup id="cite_ref-idol_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idol-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Lukaku was born in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a><sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> parents.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> His father, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Lukaku" title="Roger Lukaku">Roger Lukaku</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TDD_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDD-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> played professional football and was <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">capped</a> at international level by <a href="/wiki/DR_Congo_national_football_team" title="DR Congo national football team">Zaire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> He has a younger brother named <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Lukaku" title="Jordan Lukaku">Jordan</a>, who has progressed through the youth academy at Anderlecht<sup id="cite_ref-TDD_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDD-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and currently plays for <a href="/wiki/Royal_Antwerp_F.C." title="Royal Antwerp F.C.">Royal Antwerp</a> in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> His cousin <a href="/wiki/Boli_Bolingoli-Mbombo" title="Boli Bolingoli-Mbombo">Boli Bolingoli-Mbombo</a> plays as a left-sided winger or defender for <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul_Ba%C5%9Fak%C5%9Fehir_F.K." title="stanbul Baakehir F.K.">stanbul Baakehir</a> on loan from <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lukaku was the subject of a television documentary series called <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_School_Van_Lukaku" class="extiw" title="nl:De School Van Lukaku"><i>De School Van Lukaku</i></a> (Lukaku's School) shown on the Dutch-speaking Eén network. The reality show followed the teenage Lukaku and his classmates during the course of a year at the Saint-Guidon Institute, a school in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, where the footballer was based while with the Anderlecht youth team.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the series followed the school as it made a field trip to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, visiting Chelsea's Stamford Bridge ground. Lukaku said at the time, "What a stadium. If one day in my life I will cry, it will be the day I play here. I love Chelsea."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> In addition to his native French and Dutch, Lukaku can speak fluent English, Portuguese, Italian, Spanish and a Congolese Swahili dialect, and can also understand German.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Lukaku has stated his biggest idol was <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lukaku is a practising <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>; he made the pilgrimage to <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> He is <a href="/wiki/Teetotal" class="mw-redirect" title="Teetotal">Teetotal</a> (does not drink alcohol).<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_endorsements">Media and endorsements</span></h3>
<p>Lukaku was the first Premier League player to join Jay-Z's management agency <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation_Sports" title="Roc Nation Sports">Roc Nation Sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Lukaku signed a record sponsorship deal with German sportswear company <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma SE">Puma</a>, the company's largest endorsement deal ever.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div style=""><ol class="references" style="list-style-type:disc;">
<li id="cnote_N1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_N1_1">^</a></b></span> <div style="display:inline;" class="reference-text">Although this record was counted by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.belgianfootball.be/nl/alle-rode-duivels">RBFA</a> but Lukaku official record was 42 goals because <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> did not recognised his hat-trick goals against <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a> on 26 May 2014 due to Belgium's excessive number of <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitutions</a> in that friendly match which were not in accordance to the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">Laws of the Game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FArules_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FArules-221">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup></div></li>
<li id="cnote_N2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_N2_1">^</a></b></span> <div style="display:inline;" class="reference-text">Lukaku caps against <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a> on 14 November 2012, against <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a> (included his hat-trick goals) on 26 May 2014 and against <a href="/wiki/Czech_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech national football team">Czech Republic</a> on 5 June 2017 were counted by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.belgianfootball.be/nl/alle-rode-duivels">RBFA</a>, but not officially recognised by FIFA due to an excessive number of substitutions according to the Laws of the Game.<sup id="cite_ref-FArules_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FArules-221">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup></div></li>
</ol></div>
